The Imaginal World: Restricted and Absolute Forms
Author defines two types of imaginal world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the restricted imaginal (مثال مقيد) and the absolute imaginal (مثال مطلق) based on the role of the imaginative faculty and provide examples from Islamic tradition.

Core Idea
The imaginal world is divided by whether the imaginative faculty is required: restricted does, absolute does not.

In this passage from Bahr Ulum, the commentator introduces a division within the imaginal world that is crucial for understanding visions, dreams, and spiritual phenomena. Let's explore the definitions and examples to grasp this key distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
Find the sentence in the Arabic beginning with 'قسمان: قسم يشترط...' which explicitly divides the imaginal into two types.
2
Define restricted imaginal
This type requires the imaginative faculty; it is subjective and tied to the individual's internal imagery.
Examples include imaginative forms that may correspond or not to external reality.
3
Define absolute imaginal
This type does not require the imaginative faculty; it is objective and includes images seen in mirrors and the realm where spiritual events occur.
The passage links it to the afterlife and saintly apparitions.
4
Analyze examples
Examine each example: mirror images, resurrection of deeds, Gabriel's descent, Umar's call to Sariya (absolute); Ibrahim's vision of the ram, dreams of common people (restricted).
Note that restricted imaginal can be truthful or false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الكليات الخمس
قابل للفصل والوصل، مثل قول هذه الأجسام وهي قسمان: قسم يشترط في إدراكه القوة المخيلة، ويسمى مثالا مقيدا. وقسم لا يشترط فيه ذلك، ويسمى مثالا متفضلا، فالقسم الثاني منه الصور المرئية في المرآة وغيرها من الأجسام الثقيلة، وتتجدد فيه الأرواح، ويتروح فيه الأجساد، ويحشر فيها الموتى يوم القيامة وينعم أهل الجنة بصور أعمالهم الحسنة، ويعذب أهل النار بصور أعمالهم القبيحة ، فيظهر تلك على صورة النار فيحرقهم.
وفي هذا العالم كان ينزل جبريل على صورة دحية رضى الله عنه على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ويشهد الأولياء الخضر وغيره من الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام، لا سيما على نبينا وآله وأصحابه في هذا العالم، والنفوس الكاملة للأولياء الكرام يتشاكلون فيه بمثل أشكالهم العنصرية، فيظهرون على ما يريدون الظهور عليهم، بسبب انسلاخهم عن أبدانهم العنصرية، كظهور أمير المؤمنين عمر رض الله عنه لسارية رض الله عنه حين غلب عليه العدو، وقال: الجبل الجبل، وكان أمير المؤمنين يخطب في المدينة، كما هو مشروح في المشكاة» و«النفحات».
وبعد الموت تغلب تلك القوة، ومن المثال المقيد الصور المخيلة صورة له، لكن قد يكون غير مطابقة بحسب الظاهر ، كما رأى إبراهيم - على نبينا وآله وأصحابه وعليه السلام - الكبش في صورة إسحاق - على نبينا وآله وعليه وسلم، فمن رأى هذه الصورة فرؤياه معتبرة قطعا .
ومنه الصور المخيلة من غير مناسبة الأمر، فليس لصاحب هذه الصورة وجود في الأعيان، كأكثر الصور المرئية للمجانين والمسرسمين، والمرئية في المنامات للعامة، فمن رأى هذه الصورة فرؤياه كاذبة بيقين، ويسمى أضغاث أحلام.
الخامس: عالم الشهادة، وهو عالم الأجسام، وهي خمس عشرة كرة: العرش والكرسي، والفلك الأطلس المحدد لجهات الحركات المستقيمة، وفلك الثوابت، وهذه الأربعة بسائط لها طبيعة خامسة، غير طبائع العناصر، والسماوات السبع للسيارات، وهي مركبات من العناصر كسائر المركبات، تكونت من الدخان المرتفع، كما يشهد به نور الوحي الذي نزل على سيد المرسلين صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وكرة النار والهواء والماء والأرض، وهذه الأربعة بسائط متخالفة الطبائع، ويكون منها المركبات العنصرية، كالمعادن والنباتات والحيوانات ويطلب التفصيل من الحكمة الطبيعية، وهذه المراتب الثلاثة منسوبة إلى الكون.
السادس: الإنسان، وهو مظهر جامع لجميع المظاهر التعين الأول مع ما فيه ظهر في الثاني، وهو مع ما فيه ظهر في العوالم الثلاثة، والإنسان جامع للكل، ولذا يسمى بالعالم الصغير، وصار خليفة مسجود الملائكة، وإليه أشار الله حيث قال مخاطبا لإبليس : ﴿مَا مَنَعَكَ أَن تَسْجُدَ لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَى أَسْتَكْبَرْتَ أَمْ كُنتَ مِنَ الْعَالِينَ) [ص/ ٧٥] ، والمراد من اليدين الأوصاف الجلالية والجمالية . ولَمَّا لم يعلمه إبليس كما كان ، ولم يتفطن لسبب الخلافة حيث قال وأَنا خَيْرٌ مِّنْهُ خَلَقْتَنِي مِن نَّارٍ وَخَلَقْنَهُ مِن طِين [ص/ ٧٦]، وحسبه طينا، ولم يعلم أن جميع الأسماء والصفات جزئياتها وكلياتها غير متناهية كنونة فيه، ولم يعلم أنه جامع بين الصفات القديم والحادث استحق اللعن الأبدي.
Chapter on the five universals. It is divisible and connectable, like saying these bodies, and they are two types: a type that requires the imaginative faculty for its perception, and it is called restricted imaginal. And a type that does not require that, and it is called absolute imaginal. The second type includes images seen in mirrors and other heavy bodies. In it, spirits are renewed, bodies become spiritual, the dead are resurrected on the Day of Judgment, the people of Paradise enjoy the forms of their good deeds, and the people of Hell are punished with the forms of their evil deeds, so that appears in the form of fire and burns them. In this world, Gabriel used to descend in the form of Dihya (may Allah be pleased with him) to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). The saints witness al-Khidr and other prophets (peace be upon them), especially upon our Prophet and his family and companions, in this world. The complete souls of noble saints take on forms similar to their elemental forms, and they appear to whomever they wish to appear to, due to their detachment from their elemental bodies, like the appearance of the Commander of the Faithful, Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) to Sariya (may Allah be pleased with him) when the enemy overcame him, saying: 'The mountain! The mountain!' The Commander of the Faithful was delivering a sermon in Medina, as explained in 'al-Mishkat' and 'al-Nafahat'. After death, that power dominates. And from the restricted imaginal are the imaginative forms that have an image, but may be non-corresponding in appearance, as Ibrahim (peace be upon him and our Prophet and his companions) saw the ram in the form of Ishaq (peace be upon our Prophet and him). Whoever sees this form, his vision is definitely reliable. And from it are imaginary forms without correspondence to the matter; its owner has no existence in entities, like most images seen by the insane and those intoxicated, and seen in the dreams of common people. Whoever sees this form, his vision is definitely false, and it is called confused dreams. The fifth: the world of testimony, which is the world of bodies. They are fifteen spheres: the Throne, the Footstool, the Atlas sphere that determines the directions of rectilinear motions, the sphere of fixed stars - these four are simple, having a fifth nature different from the natures of the elements - and the seven heavens of the planets, which are compounds of elements like other compounds, formed from rising smoke, as witnessed by the light of revelation that descended upon the Master of the Messengers (peace be upon him and his family and companions). And the spheres of fire, air, water, and earth - these four are simple with differing natures, and from them arise elemental compounds like minerals, plants, and animals. Detailed explanation is sought from natural philosophy. These three levels are attributed to existence. The sixth: the human being, who is a comprehensive manifestation of all manifestations: the first determination with what appeared in it appears in the second, and what is in it appears in the three worlds. The human being encompasses everything, hence called the microcosm. He became a vicegerent prostrated to by the angels. Allah referred to this when addressing Iblis: 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My hands? Were you arrogant or of the high ones?' [Sad:75]. The meaning of 'hands' is the attributes of majesty and beauty. When Iblis did not know him as he was, and did not grasp the reason for the vicegerency, saying 'I am better than him; You created me from fire and created him from clay' [Sad:76], considering him only clay, and did not know that all names and attributes, their particulars and universals, are infinite in his existence, and did not know that he combines the attributes of the eternal and the temporal, he deserved eternal curse.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage from 'Bahr Ulum', a commentary on the logical poem 'Sullam al-'Ulum', takes a metaphysical turn. It begins by discussing the 'five universals' (الكليات الخمس), but immediately moves to an ontological classification of worlds, not logical categories. The author first describes the imaginal world (عالم المثال) in two types: restricted (مقيد) and absolute (مطلق). The restricted imaginal requires the imaginative faculty, while the absolute does not. The absolute includes images seen in mirrors and is the realm where spiritual events occur, such as the resurrection of deeds in forms. The author then elaborates on the imaginal realm's role in prophetic visions, saintly appearances (like Umar's call to Sariya), and dreams. Dreams are of two kinds: those with genuine correspondence (like Ibrahim's ram) and false dreams (أضغاث أحلام) with no corresponding reality. Next, the author lists the fifth universal: the world of testimony (عالم الشهادة), the physical cosmos of fifteen spheres including the Throne, Footstool, Atlas sphere, fixed stars, seven planetary spheres, and the four elements. These are either simple or compound, forming minerals, plants, and animals. Finally, the sixth universal is the human being (الإنسان), a microcosm that synthesizes all prior manifestations. The author uses the Quranic verse about Iblis to argue that the human combines divine attributes (jamal and jalal) and thus deserves prostration. Iblis's failure to recognize this led to his eternal curse. The passage thus reinterprets the logical 'five universals' as cosmic levels, with the human added as a sixth encompassing whole.

Key Terms
مثال مقيد
مثال مطلق
القوة المخيلة

Key Takeaway

The World of Testimony and the Human Microcosm
Author describes the physical cosmos and the human microcosm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the components of the world of testimony (عالم الشهادة) and explain how the human being is described as a microcosm synthesizing all levels.

Core Idea
The human microcosm encompasses all divine attributes and cosmic levels, making it worthy of vicegerency.

After discussing the imaginal realm, the commentator turns to the physical cosmos and the human being. The world of testimony is a detailed hierarchy of spheres, and the human is presented as the comprehensive manifestation of all prior worlds. Let's unpack these two 'universals'.

Guided Path
1
List the fifteen spheres
The passage enumerates: Throne, Footstool, Atlas sphere, sphere of fixed stars, seven planetary heavens, and the four elements. Note which are simple and which are compound.
This cosmology is based on Ptolemaic and Quranic sources.
2
Understand the human as microcosm
The human is described as a 'comprehensive manifestation' that contains all previous determinations. The Quranic verse about Iblis is used to argue that humans combine divine attributes.
This is a common Sufi idea, not standard in logic.
3
Analyze the verse
Read the verse 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My hands?' The 'hands' are interpreted as attributes of majesty and beauty.
The commentator emphasizes that Iblis missed the human's inner reality.

ومنه الصور المخيلة من غير مناسبة الأمر، فليس لصاحب هذه الصورة وجود في الأعيان، كأكثر الصور المرئية للمجانين والمسرسمين، والمرئية في المنامات للعامة، فمن رأى هذه الصورة فرؤياه كاذبة بيقين، ويسمى أضغاث أحلام.
الخامس: عالم الشهادة، وهو عالم الأجسام، وهي خمس عشرة كرة: العرش والكرسي، والفلك الأطلس المحدد لجهات الحركات المستقيمة، وفلك الثوابت، وهذه الأربعة بسائط لها طبيعة خامسة، غير طبائع العناصر، والسماوات السبع للسيارات، وهي مركبات من العناصر كسائر المركبات، تكونت من الدخان المرتفع، كما يشهد به نور الوحي الذي نزل على سيد المرسلين صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وكرة النار والهواء والماء والأرض، وهذه الأربعة بسائط متخالفة الطبائع، ويكون منها المركبات العنصرية، كالمعادن والنباتات والحيوانات ويطلب التفصيل من الحكمة الطبيعية، وهذه المراتب الثلاثة منسوبة إلى الكون.
السادس: الإنسان، وهو مظهر جامع لجميع المظاهر التعين الأول مع ما فيه ظهر في الثاني، وهو مع ما فيه ظهر في العوالم الثلاثة، والإنسان جامع للكل، ولذا يسمى بالعالم الصغير، وصار خليفة مسجود الملائكة، وإليه أشار الله حيث قال مخاطبا لإبليس : ﴿مَا مَنَعَكَ أَن تَسْجُدَ لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَى أَسْتَكْبَرْتَ أَمْ كُنتَ مِنَ الْعَالِينَ) [ص/ ٧٥] ، والمراد من اليدين الأوصاف الجلالية والجمالية . ولَمَّا لم يعلمه إبليس كما كان ، ولم يتفطن لسبب الخلافة حيث قال وأَنا خَيْرٌ مِّنْهُ خَلَقْتَنِي مِن نَّارٍ وَخَلَقْنَهُ مِن طِين [ص/ ٧٦]، وحسبه طينا، ولم يعلم أن جميع الأسماء والصفات جزئياتها وكلياتها غير متناهية كنونة فيه، ولم يعلم أنه جامع بين الصفات القديم والحادث استحق اللعن الأبدي.
Chapter on the five universals. It is divisible and connectable, like saying these bodies, and they are two types: a type that requires the imaginative faculty for its perception, and it is called restricted imaginal. And a type that does not require that, and it is called absolute imaginal. The second type includes images seen in mirrors and other heavy bodies. In it, spirits are renewed, bodies become spiritual, the dead are resurrected on the Day of Judgment, the people of Paradise enjoy the forms of their good deeds, and the people of Hell are punished with the forms of their evil deeds, so that appears in the form of fire and burns them. In this world, Gabriel used to descend in the form of Dihya (may Allah be pleased with him) to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). The saints witness al-Khidr and other prophets (peace be upon them), especially upon our Prophet and his family and companions, in this world. The complete souls of noble saints take on forms similar to their elemental forms, and they appear to whomever they wish to appear to, due to their detachment from their elemental bodies, like the appearance of the Commander of the Faithful, Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) to Sariya (may Allah be pleased with him) when the enemy overcame him, saying: 'The mountain! The mountain!' The Commander of the Faithful was delivering a sermon in Medina, as explained in 'al-Mishkat' and 'al-Nafahat'. After death, that power dominates. And from the restricted imaginal are the imaginative forms that have an image, but may be non-corresponding in appearance, as Ibrahim (peace be upon him and our Prophet and his companions) saw the ram in the form of Ishaq (peace be upon our Prophet and him). Whoever sees this form, his vision is definitely reliable. And from it are imaginary forms without correspondence to the matter; its owner has no existence in entities, like most images seen by the insane and those intoxicated, and seen in the dreams of common people. Whoever sees this form, his vision is definitely false, and it is called confused dreams. The fifth: the world of testimony, which is the world of bodies. They are fifteen spheres: the Throne, the Footstool, the Atlas sphere that determines the directions of rectilinear motions, the sphere of fixed stars - these four are simple, having a fifth nature different from the natures of the elements - and the seven heavens of the planets, which are compounds of elements like other compounds, formed from rising smoke, as witnessed by the light of revelation that descended upon the Master of the Messengers (peace be upon him and his family and companions). And the spheres of fire, air, water, and earth - these four are simple with differing natures, and from them arise elemental compounds like minerals, plants, and animals. Detailed explanation is sought from natural philosophy. These three levels are attributed to existence. The sixth: the human being, who is a comprehensive manifestation of all manifestations: the first determination with what appeared in it appears in the second, and what is in it appears in the three worlds. The human being encompasses everything, hence called the microcosm. He became a vicegerent prostrated to by the angels. Allah referred to this when addressing Iblis: 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My hands? Were you arrogant or of the high ones?' [Sad:75]. The meaning of 'hands' is the attributes of majesty and beauty. When Iblis did not know him as he was, and did not grasp the reason for the vicegerency, saying 'I am better than him; You created me from fire and created him from clay' [Sad:76], considering him only clay, and did not know that all names and attributes, their particulars and universals, are infinite in his existence, and did not know that he combines the attributes of the eternal and the temporal, he deserved eternal curse.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage from 'Bahr Ulum', a commentary on the logical poem 'Sullam al-'Ulum', takes a metaphysical turn. It begins by discussing the 'five universals' (الكليات الخمس), but immediately moves to an ontological classification of worlds, not logical categories. The author first describes the imaginal world (عالم المثال) in two types: restricted (مقيد) and absolute (مطلق). The restricted imaginal requires the imaginative faculty, while the absolute does not. The absolute includes images seen in mirrors and is the realm where spiritual events occur, such as the resurrection of deeds in forms. The author then elaborates on the imaginal realm's role in prophetic visions, saintly appearances (like Umar's call to Sariya), and dreams. Dreams are of two kinds: those with genuine correspondence (like Ibrahim's ram) and false dreams (أضغاث أحلام) with no corresponding reality. Next, the author lists the fifth universal: the world of testimony (عالم الشهادة), the physical cosmos of fifteen spheres including the Throne, Footstool, Atlas sphere, fixed stars, seven planetary spheres, and the four elements. These are either simple or compound, forming minerals, plants, and animals. Finally, the sixth universal is the human being (الإنسان), a microcosm that synthesizes all prior manifestations. The author uses the Quranic verse about Iblis to argue that the human combines divine attributes (jamal and jalal) and thus deserves prostration. Iblis's failure to recognize this led to his eternal curse. The passage thus reinterprets the logical 'five universals' as cosmic levels, with the human added as a sixth encompassing whole.

Key Terms
عالم الشهادة
الإنسان
العالم الصغير
خليفة

Key Takeaway
The human microcosm synthesizes all cosmic levels and divine attributes, justifying the unique status of vicegerent.

Conditions of a Valid Definition: Muttarid and Mun'akis
Defines conditions of definition and discusses broader definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a definition satisfies the conditions of muttarid and mun'akis, and assess the permissibility of defining by the broader.

Core Idea
A valid definition must neither include outsiders nor exclude insiders.

This passage establishes the key conditions for a sound definition: it must be coextensive (musawin) with the definiendum, meaning it must be both muttarid (excluding non-members) and mun'akis (including all members). The author then addresses a common objection – definition by example – and presents the view that defining by a broader term is permissible depending on the purpose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Find the terms 'muttarid' and 'mun'akis' in the Arabic. Notice that muttarid prevents false positives (non-members entering) and mun'akis prevents false negatives (members excluded). Together they ensure coextension.
These conditions are necessary for a definition to be sound.
2
Understand the objection
The objector points out that grammarians define 'noun' by example (like Zayd), which seems to violate coextension. Why would this be a problem? Because an example is a single instance, not a general definition.
3
Analyze the response
The author responds that definition by example is actually definition by specific resemblance (mushabaha mukhtassa). The example is meant to represent a type, not to limit the definiendum to that one instance.
This preserves the coextension condition because the example stands for a whole class.
4
Evaluate the permissibility of broader definitions
The passage then states the 'truth' (haqq): definition by the broader is permissible, depending on the purpose. Distinguish three purposes: (1) to grasp essence → full definition needed; (2) to distinguish from all others → coextensive or narrower; (3) to distinguish from some others → broader, narrower, or coextensive.
This shows that the strict coextension condition is not absolute; the purpose matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في المعرف وَلا بِالْأَخْفَى، وهذا أردأ، ومن ههنا يظهر عدم صحة التعريف الدوائر، وعدم استعمال اللفظ الوحشي والمشترك والمجاز بلا قرينة، وهذا الشرط متفق عليه بين القدماء والمتأخرين. وَلا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ مُسَاوِيًا للمعرَّف في الصدق، فَيَجِبُ الاِطِّرَادُ، أي المنع عن دخول أفراد غير المعرَّف فيه، وَالانْعِكَاسُ، أي الجمع لجميع أفراد المعرَّف كلها، فَلَا يَصِحُ التَّعْرِيفُ بِالْأَعَمِّ وَالْأَخَصَّ. ولما كان لقائل أن يقول : إن هذا منقوض بالتعريف بالمثال، كما يقول الأدباء الاسم كزيد أجاب بقوله : وَالتَّعْرِيفُ بِالْمِثَالِ تَعْرِيفٌ بِالْمُشَابَهَةِ الْمُخْتَصَّةِ، فمرادهم ما كان كزيد في الاستقلال وعدم الاقتران، هذا ما عليه المتأخرون، وَالْحَقُّ جَوَازُهُ بِالْأَعَمّ، وعليه المتقدمون، من عدم اشتراط المساواة. قالوا: إن كان الغرض تحصيل ماهية المعرف فلا يجوز إلا بجميع الأجزاء، وإن كان الغرض الامتياز عن كل ما عداه فقط فلا يجوز إلا بالمساوي أو الأخص، إن لم يكن الأعم ذاتيا له، وإن كان الغرض الامتياز عن بعض الأغيار فيجوز بالأعم والأخص والمساوي، وأما المباين فإن كان يوصل إلى الماهية فيجوز ، وإن كان يورث الامتياز فلا حجر في التعريف به، لكنه نادر جدا. ووجه حقيقة هذا المذهب ظاهر؛ فإن الحاجة إلى جميع الأقسام المذكورة ثابتة، فإسقاط البعض عن درجة الاعتبار غير لائق.
Chapter on the definer. And not by the more obscure, and this is the worst. From here appears the invalidity of circular definition, and the non-use of strange, ambiguous, and metaphorical expression without a clue. This condition is agreed upon between the earlier and later scholars. And it is necessary that the definition be coextensive with the definiendum in truth. So the condition of muttarid is necessary, meaning preventing the entry of individuals not belonging to the definiendum, and the condition of mun'akis, meaning gathering all individuals of the definiendum. So definition by the broader and the narrower is not valid. When it might be said: this is refuted by definition by example, as the grammarians say 'the noun is like Zayd,' he answered: definition by example is definition by specific resemblance, so they intend what is like Zayd in independence and lack of conjunction. This is what the later scholars hold. But the truth is its permissibility by the broader, and the earlier scholars held this, not requiring coextension. They said: if the purpose is to acquire the essence of the definiendum, it is not permissible except with all parts; if the purpose is distinction from everything else only, it is not permissible except by the coextensive or the narrower, if the broader is not essential to it; if the purpose is distinction from some others, it is permissible by the broader, narrower, and coextensive. As for the distinct, if it leads to the essence it is permissible; if it yields distinction, there is no objection to defining by it, but it is very rare. The correctness of this doctrine is apparent; for the need for all the mentioned divisions is established, so dropping some from consideration is not fitting.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage defines the conditions of a valid definition (ta'rif). It begins by stating that a definition must not be by the more obscure (akhfa), which is the worst kind. This includes avoiding circular definitions, strange words, ambiguous terms (mushtarak), and metaphorical language without context. These conditions are agreed upon by earlier and later scholars. The key condition is that the definition must be coextensive (musawin) with the definiendum in truth. This entails two properties: muttarid (preventing inclusion of non-members) and mun'akis (including all members). Thus, a definition that is broader (a'am) or narrower (akhass) than the definiendum is invalid. The author then addresses an objection: grammarians define 'noun' by example (e.g., 'like Zayd'), which seems to violate coextension. The response explains that such definition is by specific resemblance (mushabaha mukhtassa), not by true commonality. The author then presents the truth (haqq): definition by the broader is permissible, as the earlier scholars held. They distinguished three purposes: (1) if the goal is to grasp the essence, only a full definition (by all parts) works; (2) if the goal is distinction from everything else, only coextensive or narrower definition works; (3) if the goal is distinction from some others, any of broader, narrower, or coextensive may work. Even definition by something completely distinct (mubayin) is permissible if it leads to the essence or yields distinction. The correctness is shown by the need for all these types in practice.

Key Terms
المعرف
الاطراد
الانعكاس
المساواة
التعريف بالمثال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone defines 'wine' (khamr) as 'every intoxicating liquid', this definition fails which condition?
A) It fails muttarid because it includes non-wine intoxicants.
B) It fails mun'akis because it does not include all wines.
C) It fails both muttarid and mun'akis.
D) It is a valid definition.

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must be coextensive, achieving both muttarid (exclusion of non-members) and mun'akis (inclusion of all members), but the permissibility of broader definitions depends on the purpose of the definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
In a usul al-fiqh debate, someone defines 'riba' as 'excess in a sale'. Is this definition muttarid? Mun'akis? Use the three purposes to determine if it could be acceptable.

Hadd and Rasm

Hadd vs Rasm: Essential and Accidental Definitions
Distinguishes essential definition (hadd) from description (rasm) based on the nature of the distinguisher.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a hadd (essential definition) and a rasm (descriptive definition) by checking whether the distinguishing characteristic is essential or accidental to the definiendum.

Core Idea
A definition is hadd if its distinguisher is essential; if accidental, it is rasm.

The passage begins by drawing a fundamental line between two types of definitions: those that capture the essence (hadd) and those that merely describe (rasm). The criterion is whether the trait used to distinguish the thing is part of its inner reality or something external and accidental. Understanding this distinction is the first step in evaluating any definition you encounter in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the distinguisher
Find the term or phrase in the definition that is supposed to set the definiendum apart from everything else. For example, in 'human is a rational animal', the distinguisher is 'rational'.
2
Check if the distinguisher is essential (dhati) or accidental (aradi)
Ask: Does this trait necessarily flow from the thing's essence? If yes (like rationality for humans), it is essential. If it could be present or absent without changing the thing's identity (like 'laughing'), it is accidental.
The passage notes a difference between earlier and later scholars on this point, but the core test is the same.
3
Classify as hadd or rasm
If the distinguisher is essential, the definition is a hadd. If accidental, it is a rasm. The later scholars focus on the distinguisher; the earlier scholars look at whether the parts themselves are essential or accidental.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَهُوَ، أي المعرف حَدٌ، إِنْ كَانَ الْمُمَيَّزُ المذكور فيه ذاتيا للمعرَّف، وَإِلَّا يكنْ ذاتيا بل عرضيا فَهُوَ رَسْمٌ، هذا ما عليه المتأخرون، وأما على رأي القدماء إن كان بالذاتيات حد، وإن كان بالعوارض رسم، وَهُوَ تَامٌ إِنِ اشْتَمَلَ عَلَى الْجِنْسِ الْقَرِيبِ حدا كان أو رسما، وَإِلَّا يشتمل عليه فَنَاقِصٌ، فَالْحَدُّ التَّامُّ مَا اشْتَمَلَ عَلَى الْجِنْسِ وَالْفَصْلِ الْقَرِيبَيْنِ، وَهُوَ الْمُوصِلُ إِلَى الْكُنْهِ، هذا ما هو المشهور. والحق أنه ما اشتمل على جميع الأجزاء، خارجية أو عقلية، لكن المنطقيين لم يعتبروا التحديد بالأجزاء الخارجية؛ لعدم إيصاله إلى مجهول، كما سيظهر إن شاء الله تعالى سره. وَيُسْتَحْسَنُ تَقْدِيمُ الْجِنْسِ على الفصل في الحد التام، وَيَجِبُ تَقْبِيدُ أَحَدِهِمَا بِالْآخَرِ، لا على أنه خارج عنه، بل على أنه محصل لحقيقته. قال النصير الطوسي في منطق التجريد: المقومات إن لم تترتب على ترتيب، كما يقال في تعريف الإنسان ناطق حيوان كان المركب منهما رسما، فالحد عنده معرف مشتمل على جميع المقومات تركيبا طبيعيا، وقد وقع في بعض عبارات الشفاء: يجب في التحديد تقديم الجنس على الفصل، ولم يظهر لهذا العبد إلى الآن وجهه، ولعل الله يحدث بعد ذلك أمرا. وَهُوَ، أي الحد، لَا يَقْبَلُ الزِّيَادَةَ وَالنُّقْصَانَ في نفس الأمر حقيقة، وقد يضطر إليها، فيؤخذ أمر أجنبي لأجل تحصيل الحد الحقيقي، فلا بد في تحديد العرض الذاتي من أخذ المعروض، كما يقال في تحديد الزوجية انقسام العدد إلى المتساويين، وفي تحديد الأعدام من أخذ الملكات والموضوع، كما
And it (the definer) is a definition (hadd) if the distinguisher mentioned in it is essential to the definiendum; otherwise, if it is accidental, then it is a description (rasm). This is what the later scholars hold. As for the opinion of the earlier scholars: if it is by essentials, it is a hadd; if by accidents, a rasm. And it is complete (tamm) if it includes the proximate genus, whether it is a hadd or a rasm; otherwise, if it does not include it, it is incomplete (naqis). So the complete definition (hadd tamm) is what includes the proximate genus and differentia, and it is what leads to the essence (al-kunh). This is what is well-known. But the truth is that it includes all parts, whether external or mental, but the logicians did not consider definition by external parts because it does not lead to the unknown, as will appear—if Allah wills—its secret. It is recommended to present the genus before the differentia in the complete definition, and it is necessary to qualify one of them by the other, not as something external but as that which actualizes its reality. Al-Nasir al-Tusi said in Mantiq al-Tajrid: If the constituents are not arranged in order, as when it is said in the definition of human 'rational animal', the compound of them would be a rasm. So the definition according to him is a definer comprising all constituents in a natural composition. And it occurs in some expressions of al-Shifa' that it is necessary in definition to present the genus before the differentia, but this servant has not yet seen its reason; perhaps Allah will bring something later. And it (the definition) does not accept increase or decrease in reality, but sometimes one is forced to it, so an extraneous thing is taken for the sake of obtaining the real definition. So in defining an accidental attribute (al-'arad al-dhati) it is necessary to take the subject, as is said in defining parity as the division of number into two equal parts, and in defining privations by taking the possessor and the subject, as...
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage defines the types of definition. It begins by distinguishing between hadd (essential definition) and rasm (descriptive definition). According to the later scholars, if the distinguishing characteristic in the definition is essential (dhati) to the definiendum, it is a hadd; if it is accidental (aradi), it is a rasm. The earlier scholars hold that a definition by essential parts is hadd, while by accidents is rasm, regardless of the distinguisher. Next, the passage classifies definitions as complete (tamm) or incomplete (naqis). A complete definition includes the proximate genus (al-jins al-qarib), whether it is hadd or rasm; otherwise it is incomplete. A complete hadd is what includes both the proximate genus and the proximate differentia, and it leads to the essence (kunh). However, the author notes that the truth (haqq) is that a complete definition includes all parts, whether external (like matter and form) or mental (like genus and differentia), but logicians do not consider definition by external parts because it does not lead to the unknown (i.e., it does not convey new knowledge). The passage then discusses the order of genus and differentia: it is recommended to present the genus before the differentia in the complete hadd, and it is necessary to qualify one by the other (i.e., the differentia qualifies the genus) not as an external addition but as actualizing its reality. Al-Nasir al-Tusi is quoted: if the constituents are not arranged in natural order, the result is a rasm. For example, defining human as 'rational animal' without ordering genus and differentia would be a rasm; his view is that a hadd must include all constituents in a natural composition. The passage notes a discrepancy in Ibn Sina's al-Shifa' requiring the genus to precede, but Tusi does not see the reason for this. Finally, the passage states that definition does not accept increase or decrease in reality, though sometimes one is forced to include an extraneous element to achieve a real definition. Examples: defining an accidental attribute like parity requires mentioning the subject (number), and defining privations requires mentioning the possessor and the subject.

Key Terms
الحد
الرسم
المميز
ذاتي
عرضي

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does the later scholars' criterion for hadd differ from that of the earlier scholars?

B) The later scholars require the parts to be essential; the earlier scholars require the distinguisher to be essential.
C) There is no difference; both consider the same thing.
D) The later scholars consider only genus and differentia; the earlier scholars consider all parts.

Key Takeaway
The fundamental distinction between hadd and rasm hinges on whether the distinguishing characteristic is essential or accidental to the definiendum.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given the definition: 'A human is a featherless biped'. Identify whether this is a hadd or a rasm according to the criterion of the later scholars. Explain your reasoning.
?
In the definition of 'wudu' as 'washing the face and hands up to the elbows, wiping the head, and washing the feet', is the distinguisher (the specific actions) essential or accidental to the reality of wudu? Would this count as hadd or rasm?

5 min
Complete vs Incomplete Definitions (Tamm vs Naqis)
Defines complete and incomplete definitions based on inclusion of the proximate genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a definition as complete (tamm) or incomplete (naqis) by checking whether it includes the proximate genus.

Core Idea
A definition is complete only if it includes the proximate genus, whether it is hadd or rasm.

After distinguishing hadd from rasm, the passage introduces another crucial classification: completeness. A definition, regardless of whether it is essential or descriptive, is considered complete if it mentions the proximate genus—the immediate category above the species. If it omits that, it is incomplete. This classification helps evaluate how well a definition situates the definiendum in its proper place.

Guided Path
1
Find the genus (jins) mentioned in the definition
Look for the broader category that the definiendum belongs to. For example, in 'human is a rational animal', the genus is 'animal'. If the definition includes this genus, proceed to step 2.
2
Determine if the genus is the proximate genus (al-jins al-qarib)
The proximate genus is the immediate genus in the hierarchy. For example, 'animal' is the proximate genus of 'human' because there is no intermediate genus between 'animal' and 'human'. If the genus mentioned is not the proximate (e.g., 'body' for human), the definition is still incomplete because it is too broad.
3
Classify as tamm if the proximate genus is present; otherwise naqis
If the definition includes the proximate genus, it is complete (tamm). If it does not, it is incomplete (naqis). This applies to both hadd and rasm.
The passage explicitly states: 'And it is complete if it includes the proximate genus, whether it is a hadd or a rasm; otherwise, it is incomplete.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَهُوَ، أي المعرف حَدٌ، إِنْ كَانَ الْمُمَيَّزُ المذكور فيه ذاتيا للمعرَّف، وَإِلَّا يكنْ ذاتيا بل عرضيا فَهُوَ رَسْمٌ، هذا ما عليه المتأخرون، وأما على رأي القدماء إن كان بالذاتيات حد، وإن كان بالعوارض رسم، وَهُوَ تَامٌ إِنِ اشْتَمَلَ عَلَى الْجِنْسِ الْقَرِيبِ حدا كان أو رسما، وَإِلَّا يشتمل عليه فَنَاقِصٌ، فَالْحَدُّ التَّامُّ مَا اشْتَمَلَ عَلَى الْجِنْسِ وَالْفَصْلِ الْقَرِيبَيْنِ، وَهُوَ الْمُوصِلُ إِلَى الْكُنْهِ، هذا ما هو المشهور. والحق أنه ما اشتمل على جميع الأجزاء، خارجية أو عقلية، لكن المنطقيين لم يعتبروا التحديد بالأجزاء الخارجية؛ لعدم إيصاله إلى مجهول، كما سيظهر إن شاء الله تعالى سره. وَيُسْتَحْسَنُ تَقْدِيمُ الْجِنْسِ على الفصل في الحد التام، وَيَجِبُ تَقْبِيدُ أَحَدِهِمَا بِالْآخَرِ، لا على أنه خارج عنه، بل على أنه محصل لحقيقته. قال النصير الطوسي في منطق التجريد: المقومات إن لم تترتب على ترتيب، كما يقال في تعريف الإنسان ناطق حيوان كان المركب منهما رسما، فالحد عنده معرف مشتمل على جميع المقومات تركيبا طبيعيا، وقد وقع في بعض عبارات الشفاء: يجب في التحديد تقديم الجنس على الفصل، ولم يظهر لهذا العبد إلى الآن وجهه، ولعل الله يحدث بعد ذلك أمرا. وَهُوَ، أي الحد، لَا يَقْبَلُ الزِّيَادَةَ وَالنُّقْصَانَ في نفس الأمر حقيقة، وقد يضطر إليها، فيؤخذ أمر أجنبي لأجل تحصيل الحد الحقيقي، فلا بد في تحديد العرض الذاتي من أخذ المعروض، كما يقال في تحديد الزوجية انقسام العدد إلى المتساويين، وفي تحديد الأعدام من أخذ الملكات والموضوع، كما
And it (the definer) is a definition (hadd) if the distinguisher mentioned in it is essential to the definiendum; otherwise, if it is accidental, then it is a description (rasm). This is what the later scholars hold. As for the opinion of the earlier scholars: if it is by essentials, it is a hadd; if by accidents, a rasm. And it is complete (tamm) if it includes the proximate genus, whether it is a hadd or a rasm; otherwise, if it does not include it, it is incomplete (naqis). So the complete definition (hadd tamm) is what includes the proximate genus and differentia, and it is what leads to the essence (al-kunh). This is what is well-known. But the truth is that it includes all parts, whether external or mental, but the logicians did not consider definition by external parts because it does not lead to the unknown, as will appear—if Allah wills—its secret. It is recommended to present the genus before the differentia in the complete definition, and it is necessary to qualify one of them by the other, not as something external but as that which actualizes its reality. Al-Nasir al-Tusi said in Mantiq al-Tajrid: If the constituents are not arranged in order, as when it is said in the definition of human 'rational animal', the compound of them would be a rasm. So the definition according to him is a definer comprising all constituents in a natural composition. And it occurs in some expressions of al-Shifa' that it is necessary in definition to present the genus before the differentia, but this servant has not yet seen its reason; perhaps Allah will bring something later. And it (the definition) does not accept increase or decrease in reality, but sometimes one is forced to it, so an extraneous thing is taken for the sake of obtaining the real definition. So in defining an accidental attribute (al-'arad al-dhati) it is necessary to take the subject, as is said in defining parity as the division of number into two equal parts, and in defining privations by taking the possessor and the subject, as...
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage defines the types of definition. It begins by distinguishing between hadd (essential definition) and rasm (descriptive definition). According to the later scholars, if the distinguishing characteristic in the definition is essential (dhati) to the definiendum, it is a hadd; if it is accidental (aradi), it is a rasm. The earlier scholars hold that a definition by essential parts is hadd, while by accidents is rasm, regardless of the distinguisher. Next, the passage classifies definitions as complete (tamm) or incomplete (naqis). A complete definition includes the proximate genus (al-jins al-qarib), whether it is hadd or rasm; otherwise it is incomplete. A complete hadd is what includes both the proximate genus and the proximate differentia, and it leads to the essence (kunh). However, the author notes that the truth (haqq) is that a complete definition includes all parts, whether external (like matter and form) or mental (like genus and differentia), but logicians do not consider definition by external parts because it does not lead to the unknown (i.e., it does not convey new knowledge). The passage then discusses the order of genus and differentia: it is recommended to present the genus before the differentia in the complete hadd, and it is necessary to qualify one by the other (i.e., the differentia qualifies the genus) not as an external addition but as actualizing its reality. Al-Nasir al-Tusi is quoted: if the constituents are not arranged in natural order, the result is a rasm. For example, defining human as 'rational animal' without ordering genus and differentia would be a rasm; his view is that a hadd must include all constituents in a natural composition. The passage notes a discrepancy in Ibn Sina's al-Shifa' requiring the genus to precede, but Tusi does not see the reason for this. Finally, the passage states that definition does not accept increase or decrease in reality, though sometimes one is forced to include an extraneous element to achieve a real definition. Examples: defining an accidental attribute like parity requires mentioning the subject (number), and defining privations requires mentioning the possessor and the subject.

Key Terms
التام
الناقص
الجنس القريب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what makes a definition incomplete (naqis)?
A) It lacks the differentia.
B) It does not include the proximate genus.
C) It uses accidental instead of essential parts.
D) It fails to lead to the essence.

Key Takeaway
Completeness depends on whether the definition includes the proximate genus; this applies to both essential and descriptive definitions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition: 'Zakat is a financial obligation on specific wealth to be given to specific recipients.' Identify whether this definition includes the proximate genus. What is the proximate genus of zakat? Is the definition complete or incomplete according to the passage?
?
The definition 'Sawm (fasting) is abstaining from eating, drinking, and marital relations from dawn to sunset.' Does it include a genus? If not, how would you complete it?

Hadd and Rasm
beginner
5 min
The Complete Essential Definition (Hadd Tamm) and Reaching the Essence
Defines complete essential definition as containing proximate genus and differentia, leading to essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the components of a complete hadd and explain how it leads to the essence (kunh).

Core Idea
The complete hadd, containing both proximate genus and differentia, reveals the inner reality of a thing.

Having established that a complete definition includes the proximate genus, the passage now specifies what a complete essential definition (hadd tamm) comprises: both the proximate genus and the proximate differentia. Such a definition is said to lead to the essence (kunh) of the thing. This is the pinnacle of definition in Islamic logic, because it captures the thing's very quiddity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two components: proximate genus and proximate differentia
In a complete hadd, look for both the immediate genus (e.g., 'animal') and the immediate differentia (e.g., 'rational'). These together should uniquely define the species.
2
Check that both are proximate (close)
Proximate here means there is no intermediate step. For example, 'body' is not the proximate genus of human; 'animal' is. Similarly, 'sentient' is not the proximate differentia; 'rational' is.
3
Understand that this combination leads to the essence (kunh)
The passage states that the complete hadd 'leads to the essence' (al-mūṣil ilā al-kunh). This means it reveals the quiddity (mahiyya) of the thing, making known what it truly is.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Hadd and Rasm
intermediate
7 min
The Truth About Complete Definitions: Including All Parts
Contrasts well-known complete hadd with the truth that complete definitions include all parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the well-known view of the complete hadd with the position that true completeness includes all parts (external and mental).

Core Idea
A truly complete definition includes all parts, both external and mental, but logicians restrict it to mental parts for epistemological reasons.

After presenting the well-known view that a complete hadd consists of proximate genus and differentia, the author adds a deeper layer: the truth (haqq) is that a complete definition includes all parts—both external (like matter and form) and mental (genus and differentia). However, logicians avoid external parts because they do not lead from the unknown to the known. This lesson explores that nuance.

Guided Path
1
Recall the well-known view of complete hadd
The well-known view says a complete hadd includes proximate genus and differentia. The author acknowledges this as mashhur.
2
Understand the author's claim about the truth (haqq)
The author says the truth is that a complete definition includes all parts—whether external (like material components) or mental (like logical constituents). This is a more encompassing view.
3
Recognize the logicians' practical restriction
Despite this broader truth, logicians do not consider definitions using external parts because such definitions do not lead to the unknown (majhul). They aim to define by mental, essential parts that move the mind from ignorance to knowledge.
The passage says: 'the logicians did not consider definition by external parts because it does not lead to the unknown.'

Source Text

For example, defining human as 'rational animal' without ordering genus and differentia would be a rasm; his view is that a hadd must include all constituents in a natural composition. The passage notes a discrepancy in Ibn Sina's al-Shifa' requiring the genus to precede, but Tusi does not see the reason for this. Finally, the passage states that definition does not accept increase or decrease in reality, though sometimes one is forced to include an extraneous element to achieve a real definition. Examples: defining an accidental attribute like parity requires mentioning the subject (number), and defining privations requires mentioning the possessor and the subject.

Key Terms
الحق
الأجزاء الخارجية
الأجزاء العقلية
المجهول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do logicians not consider definitions that include external parts, according to the passage?
A) Because external parts are not real.
B) Because such definitions do not lead to the unknown.
C) Because external parts are impossible to know.
D) Because they prefer rasm over hadd.

Key Takeaway
True completeness includes all parts, but logicians restrict definitions to mental parts to ensure epistemic progress.

Order of Genus and Differentia in Definitions
Discusses the recommended order and mutual relation of genus and differentia in definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules that genus should precede differentia and that the differentia qualifies the genus as an actualization.

Core Idea
In a proper definition, genus comes first and the differentia qualifies it as an actualization, not an external addition.

The passage now turns to the internal structure of a complete hadd. It is recommended (yustaḥsan) that the genus be placed before the differentia. Moreover, the differentia must qualify the genus—not as something added from outside, but as that which actualizes (muhaṣṣil) the genus's potential. This reflects the view that the differentia brings the genus to its specific reality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genus and differentia in a given definition
Take a definition like 'human is a rational animal'. The genus is 'animal', the differentia is 'rational'.
2
Check if the genus appears first
The passage recommends (yustaḥsan) that the genus be presented before the differentia. In 'rational animal', the differentia comes first, which is not in accordance with the recommendation.
Al-Tusi later argues that such reversed order turns the definition into a rasm.
3
Understand that the differentia qualifies the genus as an actualization, not as an external addition
The differentia is not an external attribute tacked onto the genus; rather, it specifies the genus and makes it concrete. For example, 'rational' actualizes the potential in 'animal' to become 'human'.
The passage says: 'it is necessary to qualify one of them by the other, not as something external but as that which actualizes its reality.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَهُوَ، أي المعرف حَدٌ، إِنْ كَانَ الْمُمَيَّزُ المذكور فيه ذاتيا للمعرَّف، وَإِلَّا يكنْ ذاتيا بل عرضيا فَهُوَ رَسْمٌ، هذا ما عليه المتأخرون، وأما على رأي القدماء إن كان بالذاتيات حد، وإن كان بالعوارض رسم، وَهُوَ تَامٌ إِنِ اشْتَمَلَ عَلَى الْجِنْسِ الْقَرِيبِ حدا كان أو رسما، وَإِلَّا يشتمل عليه فَنَاقِصٌ، فَالْحَدُّ التَّامُّ مَا اشْتَمَلَ عَلَى الْجِنْسِ وَالْفَصْلِ الْقَرِيبَيْنِ، وَهُوَ الْمُوصِلُ إِلَى الْكُنْهِ، هذا ما هو المشهور. والحق أنه ما اشتمل على جميع الأجزاء، خارجية أو عقلية، لكن المنطقيين لم يعتبروا التحديد بالأجزاء الخارجية؛ لعدم إيصاله إلى مجهول، كما سيظهر إن شاء الله تعالى سره. وَيُسْتَحْسَنُ تَقْدِيمُ الْجِنْسِ على الفصل في الحد التام، وَيَجِبُ تَقْبِيدُ أَحَدِهِمَا بِالْآخَرِ، لا على أنه خارج عنه، بل على أنه محصل لحقيقته. قال النصير الطوسي في منطق التجريد: المقومات إن لم تترتب على ترتيب، كما يقال في تعريف الإنسان ناطق حيوان كان المركب منهما رسما، فالحد عنده معرف مشتمل على جميع المقومات تركيبا طبيعيا، وقد وقع في بعض عبارات الشفاء: يجب في التحديد تقديم الجنس على الفصل، ولم يظهر لهذا العبد إلى الآن وجهه، ولعل الله يحدث بعد ذلك أمرا. وَهُوَ، أي الحد، لَا يَقْبَلُ الزِّيَادَةَ وَالنُّقْصَانَ في نفس الأمر حقيقة، وقد يضطر إليها، فيؤخذ أمر أجنبي لأجل تحصيل الحد الحقيقي، فلا بد في تحديد العرض الذاتي من أخذ المعروض، كما يقال في تحديد الزوجية انقسام العدد إلى المتساويين، وفي تحديد الأعدام من أخذ الملكات والموضوع، كما
And it (the definer) is a definition (hadd) if the distinguisher mentioned in it is essential to the definiendum; otherwise, if it is accidental, then it is a description (rasm). This is what the later scholars hold. As for the opinion of the earlier scholars: if it is by essentials, it is a hadd; if by accidents, a rasm. And it is complete (tamm) if it includes the proximate genus, whether it is a hadd or a rasm; otherwise, if it does not include it, it is incomplete (naqis). So the complete definition (hadd tamm) is what includes the proximate genus and differentia, and it is what leads to the essence (al-kunh). This is what is well-known. But the truth is that it includes all parts, whether external or mental, but the logicians did not consider definition by external parts because it does not lead to the unknown, as will appear—if Allah wills—its secret. It is recommended to present the genus before the differentia in the complete definition, and it is necessary to qualify one of them by the other, not as something external but as that which actualizes its reality. Al-Nasir al-Tusi said in Mantiq al-Tajrid: If the constituents are not arranged in order, as when it is said in the definition of human 'rational animal', the compound of them would be a rasm. So the definition according to him is a definer comprising all constituents in a natural composition. And it occurs in some expressions of al-Shifa' that it is necessary in definition to present the genus before the differentia, but this servant has not yet seen its reason; perhaps Allah will bring something later. And it (the definition) does not accept increase or decrease in reality, but sometimes one is forced to it, so an extraneous thing is taken for the sake of obtaining the real definition. So in defining an accidental attribute (al-'arad al-dhati) it is necessary to take the subject, as is said in defining parity as the division of number into two equal parts, and in defining privations by taking the possessor and the subject, as...
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage defines the types of definition. It begins by distinguishing between hadd (essential definition) and rasm (descriptive definition). According to the later scholars, if the distinguishing characteristic in the definition is essential (dhati) to the definiendum, it is a hadd; if it is accidental (aradi), it is a rasm. The earlier scholars hold that a definition by essential parts is hadd, while by accidents is rasm, regardless of the distinguisher. Next, the passage classifies definitions as complete (tamm) or incomplete (naqis). A complete definition includes the proximate genus (al-jins al-qarib), whether it is hadd or rasm; otherwise it is incomplete. A complete hadd is what includes both the proximate genus and the proximate differentia, and it leads to the essence (kunh). However, the author notes that the truth (haqq) is that a complete definition includes all parts, whether external (like matter and form) or mental (like genus and differentia), but logicians do not consider definition by external parts because it does not lead to the unknown (i.e., it does not convey new knowledge). The passage then discusses the order of genus and differentia: it is recommended to present the genus before the differentia in the complete hadd, and it is necessary to qualify one by the other (i.e., the differentia qualifies the genus) not as an external addition but as actualizing its reality. Al-Nasir al-Tusi is quoted: if the constituents are not arranged in natural order, the result is a rasm. For example, defining human as 'rational animal' without ordering genus and differentia would be a rasm; his view is that a hadd must include all constituents in a natural composition. The passage notes a discrepancy in Ibn Sina's al-Shifa' requiring the genus to precede, but Tusi does not see the reason for this. Finally, the passage states that definition does not accept increase or decrease in reality, though sometimes one is forced to include an extraneous element to achieve a real definition. Examples: defining an accidental attribute like parity requires mentioning the subject (number), and defining privations requires mentioning the possessor and the subject.

Key Terms
تقديم الجنس
تقبيد
محصل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about the relationship between genus and differentia in a complete hadd?
A) They are two independent parts.
B) One qualifies the other as an external addition.
C) One qualifies the other as an actualization of its reality.
D) The differentia must precede the genus.

Key Takeaway
In a correct definition, the genus precedes the differentia, and the differentia qualifies the genus as its actualization.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Write the definition of 'sadaqah' (charity) in the recommended order: first the genus, then the differentia. For example, 'sadaqah is a voluntary gift given for the pleasure of Allah.' Check if the genus comes first.

Al-Tusi on Natural Composition of Definitions
Presents al-Tusi's view that unarranged constituents yield a rasm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a definition qualifies as a rasm according to al-Tusi's criterion of natural composition.

Core Idea
For al-Tusi, a definition lacking natural order of constituents is a rasm, not a hadd.

The passage quotes the famous logician Nasir al-Din al-Tusi from his work Mantiq al-Tajrid. He presents a stricter view: if the constituents (al-muqawwimat) of a definition are not arranged in their natural order, the resulting compound is a rasm, even if all essential parts are present. For example, 'rational animal' is a rasm because the differentia precedes the genus, violating the natural order. A true hadd must have a natural composition (tarkib tabi'i).

Guided Path
1
Recall al-Tusi's quote from the passage
Al-Tusi says: 'If the constituents are not arranged in order, as when it is said in the definition of human 'rational animal', the compound of them would be a rasm.' So order is crucial for a hadd.
2
Understand what 'natural composition' means
Natural composition (tarkib tabi'i) means the parts are arranged in the order of the ontological hierarchy: genus before differentia. This is not conventional but reflects the logical structure of reality.
3
Apply the criterion to a new definition
Take any definition and check if the genus comes first. If not, according to al-Tusi, it is a rasm. For example, 'writing animal' for a scribe would be a rasm because 'writing' (differentia) precedes 'animal' (genus).

5 min
Definition Does Not Accept Increase or Decrease
States the invariance of definition and the necessity of including subject in defining accidents and privations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a true definition cannot be altered by adding or removing elements, and recognize when an extraneous element may be added out of necessity.

Core Idea
A true definition precisely captures the essence; any alteration would misrepresent it, yet necessity may sometimes require mentioning extra features.

The passage now addresses an important principle: a definition (hadd) in itself does not admit of increase or decrease because it exactly matches the essence. However, in practice, logicians may add extraneous elements to help isolate the real definition. For example, when defining an accidental attribute, one must include the subject. This lesson clarifies the inviolability of definitional boundaries while acknowledging pragmatic adjustments.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle: definition is fixed in reality
The passage says: 'And it (the definition) does not accept increase or decrease in reality.' That means a true definition exactly corresponds to the essence. Adding or removing any part would produce a different concept.
2
Recognize the exception: forced additions for real definition
Sometimes, one is forced (yudṭarr) to include something extraneous to attain the real definition. This happens especially with definitions of accidents and privations.
3
Apply to defining accidental attributes and privations
In defining an accidental attribute (al-'araḍ al-dhātī), you must mention the subject in which it inheres. For example, to define 'parity', you say 'the division of number into two equal parts'— 'number' is the subject. Similarly, privations require the possessor and subject.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage defines the types of definition. It begins by distinguishing between hadd (essential definition) and rasm (descriptive definition). According to the later scholars, if the distinguishing characteristic in the definition is essential (dhati) to the definiendum, it is a hadd; if it is accidental (aradi), it is a rasm. The earlier scholars hold that a definition by essential parts is hadd, while by accidents is rasm, regardless of the distinguisher. Next, the passage classifies definitions as complete (tamm) or incomplete (naqis). A complete definition includes the proximate genus (al-jins al-qarib), whether it is hadd or rasm; otherwise it is incomplete. A complete hadd is what includes both the proximate genus and the proximate differentia, and it leads to the essence (kunh). However, the author notes that the truth (haqq) is that a complete definition includes all parts, whether external (like matter and form) or mental (like genus and differentia), but logicians do not consider definition by external parts because it does not lead to the unknown (i.e., it does not convey new knowledge). The passage then discusses the order of genus and differentia: it is recommended to present the genus before the differentia in the complete hadd, and it is necessary to qualify one by the other (i.e., the differentia qualifies the genus) not as an external addition but as actualizing its reality. Al-Nasir al-Tusi is quoted: if the constituents are not arranged in natural order, the result is a rasm. For example, defining human as 'rational animal' without ordering genus and differentia would be a rasm; his view is that a hadd must include all constituents in a natural composition. The passage notes a discrepancy in Ibn Sina's al-Shifa' requiring the genus to precede, but Tusi does not see the reason for this. Finally, the passage states that definition does not accept increase or decrease in reality, though sometimes one is forced to include an extraneous element to achieve a real definition. Examples: defining an accidental attribute like parity requires mentioning the subject (number), and defining privations requires mentioning the possessor and the subject.

Key Terms

العرض الذاتي
المعروض

Key Takeaway
A true definition is invariable, but in practice, extraneous elements may be added out of necessity, especially for accidents and privations.

Defining Accidents and Privations: Subject and Possessor
Provides examples of defining accidents and privations with necessary additions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a correct definition of an accidental attribute or privation by including the necessary subject or possessor.

Core Idea
To define an accident or privation, you must mention the subject it inheres in or the possession it lacks.

The passage concludes with practical examples: defining an accidental attribute like parity requires mentioning its subject (number), and defining a privation like blindness requires mentioning the possessor (sight) and the subject (eye). This lesson focuses on these special cases, showing how the principle of forced additions applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type: accidental attribute or privation
Determine whether what you are defining is an accident (like whiteness, parity) or a privation (like blindness, death). Accidents inhere in a subject; privations are absences of a trait in a subject.
2
For accidental attributes: include the subject (ma'rud)
When defining an accident, you must mention the subject in which it exists. For example, 'parity is the division of number into two equal parts'—here 'number' is the subject.
3
For privations: include the possessor (malaka) and the subject
A privation is the absence of a certain property. To define it, you need to refer to the corresponding positive property (malaka) and the subject that lacks it. For example, 'blindness is the absence of sight in an eye'.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it (the definer) is a definition (hadd) if the distinguisher mentioned in it is essential to the definiendum; otherwise, if it is accidental, then it is a description (rasm). This is what the later scholars hold. As for the opinion of the earlier scholars: if it is by essentials, it is a hadd; if by accidents, a rasm. And it is complete (tamm) if it includes the proximate genus, whether it is a hadd or a rasm; otherwise, if it does not include it, it is incomplete (naqis). 8 min
The Inviolability of Definition: No Increase or Decrease
Explains that definition must be exactly the essence, with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify what additional elements must be included in the definitions of per se accidents, privations, and relatives, and justify their inclusion.

Core Idea
A real definition is exact; any addition or subtraction destroys it.

This passage from Ibn Sina's tradition emphasizes that a true definition captures the essence without excess or deficiency. Yet, for certain categories—accidents, privations, and relatives—the definition must incorporate the subject, the opposite quality, or the related term. Understanding this preserves the integrity of definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the principle
Understand that a definition cannot be increased or decreased in reality. Adding or removing a part changes the essence, so it is forbidden.
2
Recognize when extraneous elements are allowed
Sometimes one is forced to use an extraneous element as a tool to reach the real definition. This is a means, not part of the definition itself.
Extraneous elements are permissible only as scaffolding.
3
Analyze per se accidents
In defining a per se accident like evenness, the subject (number) must be included because the accident inheres in it. Example: evenness is division of number into two equal parts.
4
Examine privations
For privations like blindness, include the disposition (sight) and the subject (one who should see) because privation is absence in a suitable subject. Example: blindness is absence of sight from one whose nature is to be sighted.
5
Distinguish genuine vs. well-known relatives
Genuine relatives require both relata, their subjects, and the cause of correlation. Well-known relatives only need the other's definition and the cause. Example: defining father (well-known) as a rational animal with masculinity from whom another rational animal is generated.
The complexity increases for genuine relatives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَهُوَ، أَيِ الْحَدُّ، لَا يَقْبَلُ الزِّيَادَةَ وَالنُّقْصَانَ فِي نَفْسِ الْأَمْرِ حَقِيقَةً، وَقَدْ يُضْطَرُّ إِلَيْهَا، فَيُؤْخَذُ أَمْرٌ أَجْنَبِيٌّ لِأَجْلِ تَحْصِيلِ الْحَدِّ الْحَقِيقِيِّ، فَلَا بُدَّ فِي تَحْدِيدِ الْعَرَضِ الذَّاتِيِّ مِنْ أَخْذِ الْمَعْرُوضِ، كَمَا يُقَالُ فِي تَحْدِيدِ الزَّوْجِيَّةِ انْقِسَامُ الْعَدَدِ إِلَى الْمُتَسَاوِيَيْنِ، وَفِي تَحْدِيدِ الْأَعْدَامِ مِنْ أَخْذِ الْمَلَكَاتِ وَالْمَوْضُوعِ، كَمَا يُقَالُ: الْعَمَى عَدَمُ الْبَصَرِ عَمَّنْ شَأْنُهُ أَنْ يَكُونَ بَصِيرًا، وَفِي تَحْدِيدِ الْمُضَافِ الْحَقِيقِيِّ مِنْ أَخْذِ ذَاتِيَّاتِهِ وَمَوْضُوعِهِ وَأَخْذِ الْمُضَافِ الْآخَرِ وَمَوْضُوعِهِ وَعِلَّةِ التَّضَايُفِ، كَمَا يُقَالُ فِي تَحْدِيدِ الْأُبُوَّةِ: إِضَافَةٌ فِي رَجُلٍ مُقَايَسَةً إِلَى إِضَافَةٍ فِي رَجُلٍ آخَرَ حَدَّثَهَا مُقَايَسَةُ الْأُولَى إِضَافَتُهُ أُولَى حَدَّثَهَا بِتَوَلُّدِ الثَّانِي مِنَ الْأَوَّلِ، وَفِي تَحْدِيدِ الْمُضَافِ الْمَشْهُورِ مِنْ أَخْذِ حَدِّ الْمُضَافِ الْآخَرِ وَعِلَّةِ التَّضَايُفِ، كَمَا يُقَالُ فِي تَحْدِيدِ الْأَبِ حَيَوَانٌ نَاطِقٌ مَعَ الذُّكُورَةِ، يَتَوَلَّدُ مِنْهُ حَيَوَانٌ نَاطِقٌ آخَرُ، وَلَا بُدَّ فِي التَّحْدِيدِ بِحَسَبِ الْحَقِيقَةِ مِنْ أَخْذِ عِلَلِهِ، وَالِاخْتِلَالُ بِأَحَدِهَا لَا يَجُوزُ، كَذَا فِي الشِّفَاءِ.
And it, i.e., the definition, does not admit increase or decrease in reality. However, one may be forced to it, so an extraneous thing is taken for the sake of obtaining the real definition. Thus, in defining a per se accident, it is necessary to include the subject, as is said in defining 'evenness': division of number into two equal parts. And in defining privations, one must take the dispositions and the subject, as is said: 'Blindness is absence of sight from one whose nature is to be sighted.' And in defining a genuine relative, one must take its essentials, its subject, the other relative, its subject, and the cause of correlation, as is said in defining fatherhood: 'a relation in a man compared to a relation in another man, which relation is caused by the comparison of the first relation being the cause of the second through the generation of the second from the first'. And in defining a well-known relative, one takes the definition of the other relative and the cause of correlation, as is said in defining 'father': 'a rational animal with masculinity, from whom another rational animal is generated.' And in definition according to reality, it is necessary to include its causes; deficiency in any of them is not permitted. Thus in al-Shifa'.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage explains that a real definition (hadd) cannot be altered by adding or removing parts; it must exactly capture the essence. However, sometimes an extraneous element is introduced as a means to arrive at the real definition. The author then provides examples from different categories. For an accidental property (al-'arad al-dhati), the subject must be included, as defining 'evenness' requires reference to number. For privations (al-'adam), one must include the opposing quality (malaka) and the subject, e.g., blindness defined as absence of sight in something that normally sees. For genuine relatives (al-mudaf al-haqiqi), the definition must include the essentials of both relatives, their subjects, and the cause of the relation, illustrated by the complex definition of fatherhood. For common relatives (al-mudaf al-mashhur), a simpler definition suffices, including the definition of the other relative and the cause. The passage concludes by emphasizing that a real definition must include all causes ('ilal) of the thing; omitting any is not allowed, citing Ibn Sina's al-Shifa'.

Key Terms
الْعَرَض الذَّاتِيّ
الْعَدَم
الْمُضَاف

C) The genus and differentia of the subject.
D) The cause of the privation.

Key Takeaway
A real definition is sacred—it cannot be altered; but for certain categories, essential accompaniments must be explicitly stated to reach the true definition.

Defining Simple and Composite Things
States rules for definability of simple and composite entities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify entities as definable or usable as definiens based on simplicity, composition, and the exception of the true species.

Core Idea
Simple entities cannot be defined but can define; composites can be defined but the true species cannot define.

In definition theory, not every term can be defined or used to define others. This lesson clarifies which entities can be defined (maḥdūd) and which can serve as definiens (ḥadd). The principle hinges on whether the entity is simple or composite, with a key exception: the true species (al-nawʿ al-ḥaqīqī). Understanding this distinction is essential for constructing valid definitions in logic and Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify simple vs. composite
A simple entity (al-basīṭ) has no parts; a composite (al-murakkab) has parts. In the text, the simple is described as lacking parts ('laysa lahū juzʾ'), so it cannot be defined by composition.
Simple here is generic; in metaphysics it may refer to the Necessary Being.
2
Determine definability of simple entities
Since a simple has no parts, it cannot be defined (lā yuḥaddu). However, it can be used as a part in defining composites (yuḥaddu bihī).
3
Determine definability of composite entities
A composite can be defined (yuḥaddu) because its parts can be enumerated. It can also be used to define other things, except for one case: the true species.
4
Recognize the exception: the true species
The true species (al-nawʿ al-ḥaqīqī) is the lowest species – it is itself a composite but cannot define any lower species because there is none. The text says 'qad lā yuḥaddu bihī, ka al-nawʿ al-ḥaqīqī'.
This is the infima species in Porphyry's tree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْبَسِيطُ لَا يُحَدُّ؛ إِذْ لَيْسَ لَهُ جُزْءٌ، وَقَدْ يُحَدُّ بِهِ، إِذَا كَانَ جُزْءًا لِشَيْءٍ آخَرَ، وَالْمُرَكَّبُ يُحَدُّ جَوَازًا، وَيُحَدُّ بِهِ، وَقَدْ لَا يُحَدُّ بِهِ، كَالنَّوْعِ الْحَقِيقِيِّ.
And the simple cannot be defined, for it has no part. And it may be used to define, if it is a part of something else. And the composite may be defined, and may be used to define, but sometimes it may not be used to define, as in the case of the true species.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage addresses the definability of simple and composite entities. A simple entity (al-basit) has no parts, so it cannot be defined by composition. However, it can serve as a defining component for other things. A composite entity (al-murakkab) can itself be defined, and can also be used as a definiens, except for the true species (al-naw' al-haqiqi), which is the ultimate species and cannot be used to define something else because it is the lowest level of classification.

Key Terms
الْبَسِيط
الْمُرَكَّب
النَّوْع الْحَقِيقِيّ

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) A privation (al-ʿadam).

Key Takeaway
Simple entities cannot be defined but can define; composites can be defined, but the true species cannot define anything lower.
